\subsection*{Introduction}\label{introduction}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Introduction}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Clustering is a process of grouping a set of data objects into
  multiple groups or clusters so that objects within a cluster have high
  similarity, but are very dissimilar to objects in other clusters.
\item
  There are a lot of areas to apply cluster analysis, such as
  collaborative filtering, outlier detection, and dynamic trend
  detection.
\item
  In this exercise, we will practice with topic clustering. In other
  words, we will group documents by topic to support navigation and
  exploration.
\item
  If you have not done yet, please review the text vectorization
  exercise: text-vectorization.qmd\#sec-lab-text-vectorization.
\end{itemize}

In this exercise, we are going to utilize a dataset distributed as a
part of the Yelp Dataset Challenge (https://www.yelp.com/dataset). This
is the same dataset you used for the data preprocessing and assignment
2. The previous dataset had attributes processed from text, while it did
not include text. In this exercise, you would directly process text.
Let's open the data. There are 1,000 tuples and 4 attributes. The names
of attributes are self-explanatory: review\_id, text, categories, and
class. You are going to work with the text attribute.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#\# Imports all necessary modules}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ pandas }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ pd}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ numpy }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ np}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ nltk, re}

\CommentTok{\# Sklearn}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.feature\_extraction.text }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ CountVectorizer, TfidfVectorizer}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ metrics}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ pprint }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ pprint}

\CommentTok{\#\# This loads the csv file from disk}
\NormalTok{yelp\_data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ pd.read\_csv(}
\NormalTok{    filepath\_or\_buffer }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{"../data/yelp\_reviews.csv"}\NormalTok{, sep }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{","}\NormalTok{, header}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{ )}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(yelp\_data.head(}\DecValTok{20}\NormalTok{))}
\CommentTok{\#\# print the dimension of the data}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(yelp\_data.shape)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsection*{Text vectorization}\label{text-vectorization-1}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Text vectorization}

You loaded the data. Now, you need to vectorize text so that they can be
used for clustering. Before vectorization, you have to preprocess text,
including tokenization, stopwords removal, and stemming.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Convert text to a list of data}
\NormalTok{data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ yelp\_data.text.values.tolist()}

\CommentTok{\# Created a list of ids}
\NormalTok{ids }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{yelp\_data.review\_id.values.tolist()}

\CommentTok{\# Remove new line characters}
\NormalTok{data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [re.sub(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}}\ErrorTok{\textbackslash{}}\StringTok{s+\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{} \textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, sent) }\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ sent }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ data]}

\NormalTok{pprint(data[:}\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#\# Conduct text preprocessing such as tokenization, stopwords removal, and stemming.}

\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ nltk.tokenize }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ word\_tokenize}

\CommentTok{\#\# tokenization}
\NormalTok{tokens }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [word\_tokenize(review) }\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ review }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ data]}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(tokens[:}\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#\# import NLTK stopwords}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ nltk.corpus }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ stopwords}
\NormalTok{stop\_words }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ stopwords.words(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}english\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\#\# following punctuations and contractions do not deliever any special meaning in text processing.}
\NormalTok{stop\_words.extend([}\StringTok{"!"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"."}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{","}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"?"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"\textquotesingle{}"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"{-}"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"("}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{")"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"\textquotesingle{}s"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"\textquotesingle{}ve"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"\textquotesingle{}m"}\NormalTok{ ])}

\CommentTok{\#\# remove stopwords}
\NormalTok{tokens\_no\_stopwords }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [[word.replace(}\StringTok{"\textquotesingle{}"}\NormalTok{,}\StringTok{""}\NormalTok{) }\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ word }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ review }\ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ word }\KeywordTok{not} \KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ stop\_words] }\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ review }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ tokens]}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(tokens\_no\_stopwords[:}\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#\# load nltk\textquotesingle{}s SnowballStemmer}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ nltk.stem.snowball }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ SnowballStemmer}
\NormalTok{stemmer }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ SnowballStemmer(}\StringTok{"english"}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\#\# stemming and normalization by converting all characters to lower cases}
\NormalTok{tokens\_stemmed }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [[stemmer.stem(word) }\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ word }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ review] }\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ review }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ tokens\_no\_stopwords ]}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(tokens\_stemmed[:}\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#\# concatenate tokens}
\CommentTok{\#\# the input for vectorizer should be in the form of a list of string}
\NormalTok{tokens\_concatenated }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}\StringTok{" "}\NormalTok{.join(token) }\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ token }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ tokens\_stemmed]}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(tokens\_concatenated[:}\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#\#define vectorizer parameters}
\NormalTok{tfidf\_vectorizer }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ TfidfVectorizer(}
\NormalTok{                                    analyzer }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}word\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{                                    max\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{0.8}\NormalTok{, }
\NormalTok{                                    max\_features}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{2000}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{                                    min\_df}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{0.05}\NormalTok{, }
\NormalTok{                                    stop\_words}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}english\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{                                    use\_idf}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{, }
\NormalTok{                                    ngram\_range}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{,}\DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{                                    token\_pattern}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}[a{-}zA{-}Z0{-}9]\{3,\}\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# num chars \textgreater{} 3}
\NormalTok{                                  )}

\NormalTok{tfidf\_matrix }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ tfidf\_vectorizer.fit\_transform(tokens\_concatenated)}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(tfidf\_matrix.shape)}

\NormalTok{terms }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ tfidf\_vectorizer.get\_feature\_names()}

\CommentTok{\#\# print features you selected.}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(terms)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#\# it is useful to know what terms are included. But knowing the real tf{-}idf values will be more helpful}
\NormalTok{review\_index }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [n }\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ n }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ ids]}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ pandas }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ pd}
\NormalTok{df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ pd.DataFrame(}
\NormalTok{tfidf\_matrix.T.todense(), index}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{terms, columns}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{review\_index)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(df.transpose())}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Great! You have applied text preprocessing and created a tf-idf term
matrix so far. As you can see, there are a few parameters you can modify
in the TfidfVectorizer, such as max\_df and min\_df. If a term occurs
too much, then the term is not unique enough to deliver any information.
These are terms such as stopwords. Also, if a term rarely occurs, then
the term does not have enough evidence to prove to be discriminative.
Therefore, changing these parameters would give you different tf-idf
matrices. Especially, the number of terms will change. For details,
please look at the documentation:
https://scikit-learn.org/stable/modules/generated/sklearn.feature\_extraction.text.TfidfVectorizer.html

\subsection*{K-means clustering}\label{k-means-clustering}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{K-means clustering}

Now, we are ready to move onto the next fun step, which is the actual
clustering using K-means algorithm. Please note that you should specify
the number of clusters (\emph{k}) to the algorithm in advance. Also,
this algorithm finds a local optimum instead of a global optimum.
Therefore it is wise to run the k-means algorithm multiple times with
different \emph{k}. We will practice this in the later part.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.cluster }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ KMeans}

\CommentTok{\#\# specify K}
\NormalTok{num\_clusters }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{5}

\NormalTok{km\_model }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ KMeans(n\_clusters}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{num\_clusters)}

\NormalTok{km\_model.fit(tfidf\_matrix)}

\CommentTok{\#\# retrieve cluster ids}
\NormalTok{clusters }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ km\_model.labels\_.tolist()}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(clusters)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Now you can see the cluster id of each review. However, this simple
number does not deliver much information useful for you to understand
the results. Therefore it might be useful if you could get
representative words for each topic (i.e., cluster id) and the
distribution of topics.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#\# Create Pandas dataframe by using the following dictionary}
\NormalTok{review }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ \{ }\StringTok{"review\_id"}\NormalTok{ : ids, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}cluster\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: clusters \}}

\NormalTok{result }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ pd.DataFrame(review, index }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [ids] , columns }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}cluster\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{])}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(result)}

\CommentTok{\# Review topics distribution across reviews}

\NormalTok{df\_topic\_distribution }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ result[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}cluster\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{].value\_counts().reset\_index(name}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{"Num Reviews"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{df\_topic\_distribution.columns }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Topic Num\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Num Reviews\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(df\_topic\_distribution)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ \_\_future\_\_ }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ print\_function}

\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Top terms per cluster:"}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{()}

\CommentTok{\# Sort cluster centers by proximity to centroid}
\NormalTok{order\_centroids }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ km\_model.cluster\_centers\_.argsort()[:, ::}\OperatorTok{{-}}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{]}

\CommentTok{\# Set the number of top keywords for each cluster}
\NormalTok{num\_top\_keywords }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{15}

\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ i }\KeywordTok{in} \BuiltInTok{range}\NormalTok{(num\_clusters):}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Cluster }\SpecialCharTok{\%d}\StringTok{ top keywords:"} \OperatorTok{\%}\NormalTok{ i, end}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{() }\CommentTok{\#add whitespace}
    
    \ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ ind }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ order\_centroids[i, :num\_top\_keywords]: }
        \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(terms[ind])}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{() }\CommentTok{\#add whitespace}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

After reviewing top keywords for each cluster, it seems that cluster 0
is about hotels, cluster 1 is about clubs or bars, and cluster 2 to 4 is
about restaurants. This result makes sense because most reviews in Yelp
are for restaurants. Then, now it is going to be important to find the
best \emph{k} for clustering because we simply assume that 5 might be a
good number of clusters. We will do it by using Silhouette measure,
which is an intrinsic measure you learned in the lecture.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ sklearn.metrics }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ silhouette\_score}

\NormalTok{sil }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ []}
\NormalTok{kmax }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{20} \CommentTok{\#\# change this value as necessary}

\CommentTok{\#\# dissimilarity would not be defined for a single cluster, thus, minimum number of clusters should be 2}
\CommentTok{\#\# increase the number of K from 2 to 20}
\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ k }\KeywordTok{in} \BuiltInTok{range}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{, kmax}\OperatorTok{+}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{):}
\NormalTok{  kmeans }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ KMeans(n\_clusters }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ k).fit(tfidf\_matrix)}
\NormalTok{  labels }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ kmeans.labels\_}
\NormalTok{  sil.append(silhouette\_score(tfidf\_matrix, labels, metric }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}euclidean\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{))}
    
\NormalTok{K }\OperatorTok{=} \BuiltInTok{range}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{, kmax}\OperatorTok{+}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.plot(K, sil, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}bx{-}\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.xlabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}k\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Silhouette score\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.title(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Silhouette Method For Optimal k\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

So, it seems that \emph{k} = 17 or 20 seems to create the best cluster.
However, you will have different results for every run, because K-means
algorithm depends on the random initial seeds. Also, there are a lot of
other measures, and they might make a different prediction. To see other
measures, please refer to the following documentation:
https://scikit-learn.org/stable/auto\_examples/cluster/plot\_kmeans\_digits.html\#sphx-glr-auto-examples-cluster-plot-kmeans-digits-py

\subsection*{Bottom-up method}\label{bottom-up-method}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Bottom-up method}

Now it is time to practice another clustering algorithm. I will leave
this to you. As mentioned in the lecture, K-means clustering is
sensitive to noisy data. According to Zipf's law, text distribution is
usually very skewed, which means a lot of outliers. Perhaps, K-means
algorithm might not be the best algorithm for topic clustering.
Agglomerative hierarchical clustering aims at finding the best step at
each cluster fusion, and our data might have an intrinsic hierarchy in
it. Think about the category of restaurants. It might starts from
\emph{Western} vs.~\emph{Eastern}. \emph{Eastern} might have
sub-categories such as \emph{Korean}, \emph{Indian}, \emph{Chineses},
\emph{Japanese}, and so on. If the data has a hierarchy like this,
probably hierarchical clustering might be a better choice. Go for it and
see whether it really makes any difference. Please see the following
link for implementation:
https://scikit-learn.org/stable/modules/clustering.html\#hierarchical-clustering

\subsection*{References:}\label{references-4}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{References:}

https://scikit-learn.org/stable/modules/clustering.html\#k-means
http://brandonrose.org/clustering
https://www.machinelearningplus.com/nlp/topic-modeling-gensim-python/

\section*{Objectives}\label{objectives-1}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Objectives}

\markright{Objectives}

This exercise is to process a small collection of course titles (as text
documents) and compute the following statistics:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Term Frequencies (TF) of terms in each document.
\item
  Inverse Document Frequencies (IDF) of terms in the entire collection.
\end{enumerate}

\section*{1. Data}\label{data-2}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{1. Data}

\markright{1. Data}

We have a small collection of 3 course titles:

\begin{verbatim}
1 Information and System
2 Data and Information
3 System and System Programming
\end{verbatim}

\section*{\texorpdfstring{2. Create a \emph{Course}
class}{2. Create a Course class}}\label{create-a-course-class}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{2. Create a \emph{Course} class}

\markright{2. Create a \emph{Course} class}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{class}\NormalTok{ Course: }
    \KeywordTok{def} \FunctionTok{\_\_init\_\_}\NormalTok{(}\VariableTok{self}\NormalTok{, course\_id):}
        \CommentTok{\# create a new course with an ID}
        \VariableTok{self}\NormalTok{.}\BuiltInTok{id} \OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ course\_id}
        \CommentTok{\# create an empty dictionary }
        \CommentTok{\# to hold term frequency (TF) counts}
        \VariableTok{self}\NormalTok{.tfs }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ \{\}}
    
    \KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ count\_words(}\VariableTok{self}\NormalTok{, text):}
        \CommentTok{\# split a title into words, }
        \CommentTok{\# using space " " as delimiter}
\NormalTok{        words }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ text.lower().split(}\StringTok{" "}\NormalTok{)}
        \ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ word }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ words: }
            \CommentTok{\# for each word in the list}
            \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ word }\KeywordTok{in} \VariableTok{self}\NormalTok{.tfs: }
                \CommentTok{\# if it has been counted in the TF dictionary}
                \CommentTok{\# add 1 to the count}
                \VariableTok{self}\NormalTok{.tfs[word] }\OperatorTok{=} \VariableTok{self}\NormalTok{.tfs[word] }\OperatorTok{+} \DecValTok{1}
            \ControlFlowTok{else}\NormalTok{:}
                \CommentTok{\# if it has not been counted, }
                \CommentTok{\# initialize its TF with 1}
                \VariableTok{self}\NormalTok{.tfs[word] }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{1}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section*{NOW OUTSIDE THE COURSE
CLASS}\label{now-outside-the-course-class}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{NOW OUTSIDE THE COURSE CLASS}

\markright{NOW OUTSIDE THE COURSE CLASS}

\subsection*{\texorpdfstring{3. Create a \texttt{print\_dictionary}
function}{3. Create a print\_dictionary function}}\label{create-a-print_dictionary-function}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{3. Create a \texttt{print\_dictionary}
function}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ print\_dictionary(dict\_data):}
    \CommentTok{\# print all key{-}value pairs in a dictionary}
    \ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ key }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ dict\_data: }
        \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(key, dict\_data[key])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsection*{4. Steps to Vectorize the Course
Titles}\label{steps-to-vectorize-the-course-titles}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{4. Steps to Vectorize the Course
Titles}

\subsubsection*{4.1 Create an empty list of
courses}\label{create-an-empty-list-of-courses}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{4.1 Create an empty list of
courses}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{courses }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ []}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsubsection*{4.2 Create a list of the 3 course
titles}\label{create-a-list-of-the-3-course-titles}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{4.2 Create a list of the 3 course
titles}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{titles }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}\StringTok{"Information and System"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Data and Information"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"System and System Programming"}\NormalTok{]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsubsection*{4.3 Use a loop to process
data}\label{use-a-loop-to-process-data}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{4.3 Use a loop to process data}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Create a Course object for each title;
\item
  Process the title and run the TF counts;
\item
  Add the Course object (with TF statistics) to the list
  \texttt{courses}.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ i }\KeywordTok{in} \BuiltInTok{range}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{, }\BuiltInTok{len}\NormalTok{(titles)):}
\NormalTok{    title }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ titles[i]}
    
    \CommentTok{\# create a new course with an ID}
\NormalTok{    course }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ Course(i}\OperatorTok{+}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{)}
    
    \CommentTok{\# process title and compute term frequencies (TF)}
\NormalTok{    course.count\_words(title)}
    
    \CommentTok{\# add the course to the list}
\NormalTok{    courses.append(course)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsubsection*{4.4 Create an empty dictionary to keep track of DF
values}\label{create-an-empty-dictionary-to-keep-track-of-df-values}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{4.4 Create an empty dictionary to
keep track of DF values}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{dfs }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ \{\}}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsubsection*{4.5 Go through the Courses' TF dictionaries to get DF
values}\label{go-through-the-courses-tf-dictionaries-to-get-df-values}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{4.5 Go through the Courses' TF
dictionaries to get DF values}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ course }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ courses: }
    \ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ word }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ course.tfs: }
        \CommentTok{\# add 1 to DF count if the word appears in a doc (TF)}
\NormalTok{        dfs[word] }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ dfs.get(word,}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{) }\OperatorTok{+} \DecValTok{1}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsubsection*{4.6 Print DF (Document Frequency)
Statistics}\label{print-df-document-frequency-statistics}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{4.6 Print DF (Document Frequency)
Statistics}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"DF statistics: "}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"=============="}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{print\_dictionary(dfs)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsubsection*{4.7 Print TF (Term Frequency)
Statistics}\label{print-tf-term-frequency-statistics}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{4.7 Print TF (Term Frequency)
Statistics}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"TF statistics: "}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"=============="}\NormalTok{)}
\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ course }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ courses: }
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"COURSE \#}\SpecialCharTok{\{0\}}\StringTok{"}\NormalTok{.}\BuiltInTok{format}\NormalTok{(course.}\BuiltInTok{id}\NormalTok{))}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}{-}"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    print\_dictionary(course.tfs)}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{""}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section*{Objectives}\label{objectives-2}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Objectives}

\markright{Objectives}

This assignment is to process a collection of text files (documents) and
compute the following statistics:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Term Frequencies (TF) of terms in each document.
\item
  Inverse Document Frequencies (IDF) of terms in the entire collection.
\end{enumerate}

\section*{A. Data Files (1 point)}\label{a.-data-files-1-point}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{A. Data Files (1 point)}

\markright{A. Data Files (1 point)}

Please collect about \textbf{20 text data instances} (e.g.~brief news
reports or research abstracts) and save them as individual .txt files.
Files names should be named in a sequential order such as 1.txt, 2.txt,
3.txt, \ldots{} and 20.txt.

\section*{\texorpdfstring{B. Create a \emph{Document} abstract data
type/class (2
points)}{B. Create a Document abstract data type/class (2 points)}}\label{b.-create-a-document-abstract-data-typeclass-2-points}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{B. Create a \emph{Document} abstract data
type/class (2 points)}

\markright{B. Create a \emph{Document} abstract data type/class (2
points)}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{class}\NormalTok{ Document: }
    \CommentTok{"""}
\CommentTok{    The Document class to be implemented. }
\CommentTok{    Please define all required methods }
\CommentTok{    within the class structure. }
\CommentTok{    """}
    \KeywordTok{def} \FunctionTok{\_\_init\_\_}\NormalTok{(}\VariableTok{self}\NormalTok{, doc\_id):}
        \CommentTok{"""to be implemented"""}
    
    \KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ tokenize(text):}
        \CommentTok{"""to be implemented"""}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

The \texttt{Document} class should have:

\begin{itemize}
\item
  A \texttt{\_\_init\_\_(self,\ doc\_id)} method as the constructor
  method

  \begin{enumerate}
  \def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Assign \texttt{doc\_id} to \texttt{self.id}
  \item
    Create an empty \textbf{dictionary variable} with
  \end{enumerate}

  \texttt{self.variable\_name}

  Later you will keep track of all unique words and their frequencies in
  the document.
\item
  A \texttt{tokenize(text)} method that:

  \begin{enumerate}
  \def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Splits text into single words using \texttt{space} and
    \texttt{punctuation} as delimiter;
  \item
    Use a loop to go through all the words, and for each word:

    \begin{itemize}
    \tightlist
    \item
      Convert the word to lower case using the \texttt{lower()} method
      of a string;
    \item
      If it does not appear in the dictionary, add it to the dictionary
      and set its count/frequency to 1;
    \item
      If it is already in the dictionary, increment its count/frequency
      by adding 1 to it;
    \end{itemize}
  \end{enumerate}
\end{itemize}

Hint: See the lecture on data structures and follow the \emph{radish
vote couting} example.

\section*{C. NOW OUTSIDE THE DOCUMENT
CLASS}\label{c.-now-outside-the-document-class}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{C. NOW OUTSIDE THE DOCUMENT CLASS}

\markright{C. NOW OUTSIDE THE DOCUMENT CLASS}

\subsection*{\texorpdfstring{C1. Create a \texttt{save\_dictionary}
function (1
points)}{C1. Create a save\_dictionary function (1 points)}}\label{c1.-create-a-save_dictionary-function-1-points}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{C1. Create a \texttt{save\_dictionary}
function (1 points)}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ save\_dictionary(dict\_data, file\_path\_name):}
    \CommentTok{"""Saves dictionary data to a text file. }
\CommentTok{    Arguments: }
\CommentTok{        dict\_data: a dictionary with key{-}value pairs}
\CommentTok{        file\_path\_name: the full path name of a text file (output)}
\CommentTok{    """}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

The function should accept \textbf{two arguments}:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  One argument for the dictionary with data to be saved;
\item
  Second argument about the file pathname to save the data;
\end{enumerate}

The function saves all data/statistics in the dictionary to text files,
with each key-value pair in one text line separated by a tab (``\t").

The output file should look like:

\begin{verbatim}
Key1 value1
Key2 value2
Key3 value3
.. ..
\end{verbatim}

\subsection*{\texorpdfstring{C2. Create a \texttt{vectorize} function (5
points)}{C2. Create a vectorize function (5 points)}}\label{c2.-create-a-vectorize-function-5-points}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{C2. Create a \texttt{vectorize}
function (5 points)}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{def}\NormalTok{ vectorize(data\_path):}
    \CommentTok{"""Vectorizes text files in the path. }
\CommentTok{    Arguments: }
\CommentTok{        data\_path: the path to the directory (folder) where text files are}
\CommentTok{    """}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

The function should:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Take a \textbf{string argument} as the path (folder) to where the text
  data files are;
\item
  Process all data files in the path and produces TF and DF statistics;
\end{itemize}

Here are steps in the function:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\item
  Create a \textbf{dictionary variable} (this is a \textbf{global
  dictionary variable} outside the class) to keep track all unique words
  and their DF (document frequency) values;
\item
  Create a loop to go through every \textbf{.txt} files in the path
  argument. File names should be: \texttt{1.txt}, \texttt{2.txt},
  \ldots, \texttt{20.txt}.
\item
  \textbf{For each} .txt file (within the loop):

  \begin{itemize}
  \item
    Create a Document object (based on the Document class) using the
    filename as \texttt{doc\_id} parameter. For example, doc\_id should
    be \texttt{2} for \texttt{2.txt}.
  \item
    Read the content (text lines) from the text file.
  \item
    Call the document object's \texttt{.tokenize()} function to process
    the text content.
  \item
    Call the \texttt{save\_dictionary()} function to save the document's
    dictionary with TF (term frequencies) to a file, where the filename
    should be \texttt{tf\_DOCID.txt} in the same path.

    \begin{itemize}
    \item
      The TF dictionary can be accessed via the \textbf{document
      object's} \texttt{.dictionary\_variable\_name}.
    \item
      For example, after processing 1.txt file, the data should be saved
      to \texttt{tf\_1.txt} file in the same directory.
    \end{itemize}
  \item
    Create a \textbf{nested loop} (a smaller/indented loop inside the
    above loop), and \textbf{for each word in the document's
    dictionary}:

    \begin{itemize}
    \tightlist
    \item
      If it does not appear in the \textbf{dictionary for DF}
      (\textbf{the dictionary variable outside class}), then add the
      word to the DF dictionary;
    \item
      If it is already in the DF dictionary, increment its DF value by
      adding 1 to itself;
    \end{itemize}
  \end{itemize}
\item
  After all files are processed (\textbf{OUTSIDE the BIG LOOP above}),
  call the \texttt{save\_dictionary()} function \textbf{again} to save
  the DF dictionary to a file named \texttt{df.txt} in the same path
  with the input text files.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{C3. Finally, call the vectorize function (1
point)}\label{c3.-finally-call-the-vectorize-function-1-point}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{C3. Finally, call the vectorize
function (1 point)}

For example, suppose all text files are in the same directory as your
code (notebook):

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{vectorize(}\StringTok{"./"}\NormalTok{)    }\CommentTok{\# to process text files in the current irectory/folder}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section*{Bonus (optional, +1 point)}\label{bonus-optional-1-point}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Bonus (optional, +1 point)}

\markright{Bonus (optional, +1 point)}

Compute pair-wise cosine similarities among the documents using Term
Frequency (TF) weights, and save the results to a file.

Your outuput may look like (\texttt{id1\ id2\ score}):

\begin{verbatim}
1 2 0.37
1 3 0.12
1 4 0.98
. . ....
18 19 0.33
18 20 0.57
19 20 0.49
\end{verbatim}

\section*{A. Data Preparation (1
points)}\label{a.-data-preparation-1-points}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{A. Data Preparation (1 points)}

\markright{A. Data Preparation (1 points)}

Please identify or prepare a text classification dataset. You can
either: + Find and download an \textbf{existing dataset}, OR +
\textbf{Create a dataset} on your own

Some of the websites to search for a dataset: +
https://www.kaggle.com/datasets +
https://archive.ics.uci.edu/ml/datasets.php +
https://vincentarelbundock.github.io/Rdatasets/datasets.html

Specific \textbf{requirements} of your dataset: 1. {[} {]} It has to
have \textbf{text} data, e.g.~abstracts, news reports. 2. {[} {]} It has
to have a \textbf{class} attribute, e.g.~with at least \textbf{two}
categories or labels. 3. {[} {]} It has to have at least: + If it is an
\textbf{existing dataset, 300+} data instances total and \textbf{100+}
in each class, \textbf{OR} + If you \textbf{create} the dataset,
\textbf{30+} data instances total and \textbf{10+} in each class. 4. {[}
{]} Please \textbf{avoid} any dataset already used in \textbf{existing}
exercises or assignments in this class.

Please do: + {[} {]} Include a \textbf{link} to your data or
\textbf{submit} your data. + {[} {]} Include a \textbf{brief
description} of your data, attributes, and instances. + {[} {]} Discuss
the classification \textbf{task} on the data and \textbf{objectives}.

\section*{B. Probabilities and Zipf (3
points)}\label{b.-probabilities-and-zipf-3-points}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{B. Probabilities and Zipf (3 points)}

\markright{B. Probabilities and Zipf (3 points)}

\subsection*{B.1. Class Distributions and Probabilities (0.5
point)}\label{b.1.-class-distributions-and-probabilities-0.5-point}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{B.1. Class Distributions and
Probabilities (0.5 point)}

Find out the number of instances in each class \(c\) and compute it's
probability \(p(c)\). Compile a table like this (example):

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Class \(c\) & Instances \(n_c\) & Probability \(p(c)\) \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Fake & 100 & \(\frac{100}{300} = 1/3\) \\
True & 200 & \(\frac{200}{300} = 2/3\) \\
\end{longtable}
}

\subsection*{B.2. Term Probabilities and Zipf's Law (2.5
points)}\label{b.2.-term-probabilities-and-zipfs-law-2.5-points}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{B.2. Term Probabilities and Zipf's Law
(2.5 points)}

Conduct analysis in the following steps to obtain the term probability
pattern in your text data. You can follow the example in
\href{../demo/data_prob_linear.html}{Probability and Linearity in Data}
to use \texttt{CountVectorizer} from
\texttt{sklearn.feature\_extraction.text}.

\subsubsection*{B.2.1. Rank, Frequency, and
Probability}\label{b.2.1.-rank-frequency-and-probability}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{B.2.1. Rank, Frequency, and
Probability}

Rank terms by frequency and show the top five with probabilities
(example):

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lllll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
& t & \(k_t\) & \(f_t\) & \(p_t\) \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
0 & to & 1 & 2242 & \\
1 & you & 2 & 2240 & \\
2 & the & 3 & 1328 & \\
3 & and & 4 & 979 & \\
4 & in & 5 & 898 & \\
\end{longtable}
}

\subsubsection*{B.2.2. Probability vs.~Rank
Plot}\label{b.2.2.-probability-vs.-rank-plot}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{B.2.2. Probability vs.~Rank Plot}

Produce a probability \(p_t\) vs.~\(k_t\) plot on \textbf{log-log}
coordinates.

\subsubsection*{B.2.3. Regression line}\label{b.2.3.-regression-line}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{B.2.3. Regression line}

Use linear regression to fit the \(log(p_t) \sim log(k_t)\) relation: 1.
Identify the \textbf{coefficient} value from the regression, e.g.~a
value like \(-1.2\) means \(p_t \propto \frac{1}{k_t^{1.2}}\). 2. Plot
the regression line on the \(p_t\) vs.~\(k_t\) plot. 3. Do your data
follow Zipf's law? Discuss the visual pattern, the fitted coefficient,
and the regression line.

\section*{C. Text Vectorization (2
points)}\label{c.-text-vectorization-2-points}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{C. Text Vectorization (2 points)}

\markright{C. Text Vectorization (2 points)}

\subsection*{C.1. Training and Test
Data}\label{c.1.-training-and-test-data}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{C.1. Training and Test Data}

Split your data into \(80\%\) training and \(20\%\) test data.

\subsection*{C.2. Text Vectorization}\label{c.2.-text-vectorization}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{C.2. Text Vectorization}

Use the \texttt{CountVectorizer} to: 1. {[} {]} Vectorize (fit) your
\textbf{training} data, based on the \texttt{text} field. 2. {[} {]}
Your vectorizer should now have a set of \textbf{features} (words) from
the training data 3. {[} {]} Transform your \textbf{test} data (text
field), with the same vectorizer.

\subsection*{C.3. Terms and Conditional
Probabilities}\label{c.3.-terms-and-conditional-probabilities}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{C.3. Terms and Conditional
Probabilities}

\textbf{Think} about two terms (words): 1. {[} {]} One term (word)
\(t_1\) that is relevant to one class \(c_1\), e.g.~\texttt{prize} for a
\textbf{spam} class for spam classification. 2. {[} {]} A second term
(word) \(t_2\) that is relevant to another class \(c_2\).

Identify their conditional probabilities:

\begin{eqnarray}
p(t_1|c_1) & = & ... \\
p(t_1|c_2) & = & ... \\
p(t_2|c_1) & = & ... \\
p(t_2|c_2) & = & ... \\
\end{eqnarray}

Discuss and explain: 1. {[} {]} What do these probabilities mean? 2. {[}
{]} Are the above probability values reasonable (sensible)? Why or why
not? 3. {[} {]} Do you think they will be helpful in the classification
task?

\subsubsection*{D.2.1. Linearity}\label{d.2.1.-linearity}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{D.2.1. Linearity}

Remember the two terms \(t_1\) and \(t_2\) for two classes \(c_1\) and
\(c_2\) you picked earlier?

Scatter plot the training data with:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  ☐ \(t_1\) and \(t_2\) as the \(X\) and \(Y\) axes.
\item
  ☐ \textbf{Color code} data points based on their classes \(c_1\) and
  \(c_2\).

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    You only need to plot data in the two classes.
  \item
    Make sure the two colors are distinguishable.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  ☐ Discuss whether:

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    The two classes are (roughly) \textbf{separable} on the plot?
  \item
    The two classes are \textbf{linearly} separable on the plot?
  \item
    (Optional) It is possible they are linearly separable in a higher
    dimensional space with \textbf{all term features}?
  \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

\section*{Recovered retrieval questions and
exercise}\label{sec-pr-12-recovered-exercise}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Recovered retrieval questions and
exercise}

\markright{Recovered retrieval questions and exercise}

\section*{Recovered questions}\label{recovered-questions}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Recovered questions}

\markright{Recovered questions}

I do want to stress the key advantage AND disadvantage of normalization,
which is to treat terms of different forms as the same.

1) There are situations in which the different variations are indeed
about the same and should be treated as one term. This way, users who
uses one variation in the query may be able to find documents containing
terms in another.

2) But there are also situations where normalization is an
over-treatment and can lead to results that are in fact not relevant
(false positives). There are plenty of examples in both 1) and 2). In
specific domains, there might be more in 1) vs.~2), or vise versa. By
examining your domain data and use cases, you may find whether it is
better to do certain normalization or not (e.g.~casefolding, but not
stemming).

Now, we have increasingly more storage and computing power at a cheaper
price. So often we can do more with these technologies. For example, it
is common to have multiple indices even for the same data, e.g.~one with
certain normalization and one without. Then at search time, you combine
evidence from all indices to final matching and ranking of results.

We know terms have different discriminative powers -- that some terms
are more useful than the others. We know stopwords (highly frequent
terms) are generally less useful. What about rare terms, i.e., terms
that are used in a very tiny portion of documents? What about terms in
between (neither rare or too frequent)? If you have to choose a limited
number of terms to index your documents, what kind of terms would you
pick?

In the vector space model, cosine similarity is often used to measure
how close (or distant) two vectors are? For example, you can compare a
query (vector) with each document (vector), and rank them according to
their cosine similarities. Given that cosine is about the angle (vector
directions) and disregards vector magnitude (length), why is vector
direction more important than magnitude here (for term-based text
representation)?

Your analogue is good in that both "generators" are in a dynamic process
of generating something, which can trap a crawler in their space (in
both worlds).

The generator here in the context of the web is a general reference to
dynamic web pages that generate page contents based on different given
parameters.

An example of this is ﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿the "next page" link to help users navigate to
additional lists of information. An ordinary user may click on "next",
and "next", ... for a few iterations.

But a spider, without sufficient intelligence and design, may go on and
on by simply "clicking" on (following) the "next page" link nonstop...
The notion of "trap" goes both ways -- it traps the crawler on the site
gathering data on and on; but it also leads to intensive load on the
generator (as there appear to be lots of clicks and page loads to the
web server). Years ago when I was a graduate student, I developed a
crawler with an aim to collect all web pages of the entire university
(where I was studying) and, the first night I ran it, it was able to
collect 2 million+ pages with a cost. The crawler was trapped by another
college/school's site with a page "generator" and, in the end, brought
the entire server down... You can imagine what happened the next morning
when the IT manager found out... And it did take me some time to settle
the issue as as a student. ;)

Good question.

For website or pages that no one knows and links to, crawlers won't be
able to collect them. A ﻿crawler starts with seed websites (those ﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿already
known) and, ultimately, will get to those where there is a path. But
there are "islands" to which there is no path. There are also pages that
can be reached from certain parts of the web and cannot be reached
either unless you have seeds to crawl from specific locations...

There is always a part of the web where crawlers cannot ﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿﻿penetrate. We
generally refer to this as the deep web. There are private sites, sites
with access control, and sites that can be interacted with but too
difficult for crawler to collect... they represent a space much much
greater than the regular web covered by search engines. ﻿

\section*{Recovered retrieval
calculation}\label{recovered-retrieval-calculation}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Recovered retrieval calculation}

\markright{Recovered retrieval calculation}

Assume we have a tiny collection of two documents with the following
terms: Doc 1: apple, pear, dessert, cream, cook, work, berry Doc 2:
work, computer, disk, apple, network, system Given a free text query
"apple computer," rank the documents using Dice's coefficient. Please
provide the formula and list calculation steps.

Which ones (more than one) of the following statements about Euclidean
distance are true? It measures that distance between the end points of
two vectors. It measures that angle between two vectors. Euclidean
distance is affected by vector magnitudes. Euclidean distance is zero
when two vectors point to the same direction.

Which ones (more than one) of the following statements about Cosine
similarity are true? It measures that distance between the end points of
two vectors. It measures that angle between two vectors. Cosine is
affected by vector magnitudes. Cosine is 1 (max value) when two vectors
point to the same direction.

Does vector length normalization (dividing a vector by its
length/magnitude) have any impact on Cosine ranking?

\chapter*{SQLite and Data Retrieval

\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{SQLite and Data Retrieval Assignment}

\markboth{SQLite and Data Retrieval Assignment}{SQLite and Data
Retrieval Assignment}

\section*{Recovered activity}\label{sec-lab-sqlite-assignment}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Recovered activity}

\markright{Recovered activity}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, arc=.35mm, bottomrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, breakable, colback=white, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-note-color!10!white, colframe=quarto-callout-note-color-frame, coltitle=black, left=2mm, leftrule=.75mm, opacityback=0, opacitybacktitle=0.6, rightrule=.15mm, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-note-color}{\faInfo}\hspace{0.5em}{Historical source and execution note}, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, toptitle=1mm]

This activity was recovered from \texttt{problems/python\_sqlite.ipynb}.
Its code is preserved but is not executed during the public book build,
so readers can inspect it without requiring legacy package versions.
Download the \href{../notebooks/sqlite-assignment.ipynb}{source
notebook} to run and modernize it interactively.

\end{tcolorbox}

This assignment is to load data from CSV, populate them in an SQLite
database, and run in-database analytics with SQL.

Please create a Jupyter Notebook for this assignment.

\section*{A. Data}\label{a.-data}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{A. Data}

\markright{A. Data}

The data is provided as \href{../data/CCSubset.csv}{CCSubset.csv}, which
is a subset of the UCI Credit Card data set. You only need to use this
provided subset for the assignment.

Please open and review the data file
\href{../data/CCSubset.csv}{CCSubset.csv} to determine the following
when creating your table structure: 1. The name of the table: please use
a name with \textbf{NO Space} in it. 2. How many fields (columns) do you
have and what are they? 3. What are their field types?

The full dataset is available at:
https://www.kaggle.com/uciml/default-of-credit-card-clients-dataset.

\section*{B. SQLite Database Schema (2
points)}\label{b.-sqlite-database-schema-2-points}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{B. SQLite Database Schema (2 points)}

\markright{B. SQLite Database Schema (2 points)}

Make sure you import sqlite3 module by:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ sqlite3}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Create a new database, connect to it, and create a table structure
corresponding to data fields in the CSV data source.

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Use \texttt{sqlite3.connect(“DatabaseFileName”)} to connect the
  database and once you establish the connection, use its
  \texttt{.cursor()} method to maintain the cursor. For example:
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{my\_connection }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ sqlite3.}\ExtensionTok{connect}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"../data/mydatabase.db"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{my\_cursor }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ my\_connection.cursor()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Use the cursor's \texttt{.execute()} method to run SQL statements;
\item
  Use \texttt{CREATE\ TABLE} statement as a parameter for the
  \texttt{execute()} method to create a new table.
\end{itemize}

Syntax of the \texttt{create\ table} statement in SQL:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{CREATE} \KeywordTok{TABLE}\NormalTok{ table1 (}
\NormalTok{    field1 }\DataTypeTok{int} \KeywordTok{primary} \KeywordTok{key}\NormalTok{, }
\NormalTok{    field2 }\DataTypeTok{varchar}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{100}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    field3 }\DataTypeTok{numeric}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section*{C. Load Data into SQLite (2
points)}\label{c.-load-data-into-sqlite-2-points}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{C. Load Data into SQLite (2 points)}

\markright{C. Load Data into SQLite (2 points)}

Read data from the CSV file, use a loop to read each CSV line (data
instance), and insert it into the SQLite table:

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Include \texttt{import\ csv} so you can use CSV-related functions;
\item
  Please use the following program structure to read CSV data:
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ControlFlowTok{with} \BuiltInTok{open}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}students.csv\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{) }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ csvfile:}
\NormalTok{    reader }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ csv.DictReader(csvfile)}
    \ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ row }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ reader:}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Inside the loop:

\begin{itemize}
\item
  You can use
  \texttt{row{[}\textquotesingle{}CSVColumnName\textquotesingle{}{]}} to
  read each column value;
\item
  Execute a SQL statement using \texttt{INSERT\ INTO}, combined with
  data from CSV, for example, within the for loop:
\end{itemize}

Example:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{sql }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{"INSERT INTO table1 (field1, field2, field3)"} \OperatorTok{\textbackslash{}}
        \StringTok{" VALUES(}\SpecialCharTok{\{0\}}\StringTok{, \textquotesingle{}}\SpecialCharTok{\{1\}}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}, }\SpecialCharTok{\{2\}}\StringTok{)"}\NormalTok{.}\BuiltInTok{format}\NormalTok{(row[}\StringTok{"column1"}\NormalTok{], row[}\StringTok{"column2"}\NormalTok{], row[}\StringTok{"column3"}\NormalTok{])}
\NormalTok{my\_cursor.execute(sql)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Change (and add) names such as \texttt{field1/2/3/...} and
\texttt{column1/2/3/...} to the correct ones in database and CSV
respectively.

\section*{D. In-database Query and Analytics with SQLite Data (6
points)}\label{d.-in-database-query-and-analytics-with-sqlite-data-6-points}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{D. In-database Query and Analytics with
SQLite Data (6 points)}

\markright{D. In-database Query and Analytics with SQLite Data (6
points)}

Outside the previous structure, create code in Python with related SQL
statements to do the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\item
  \texttt{Update} the data so that current marriage=2 (single) and
  marriage=3 values (others) are merged/updated to 2 (single).
\item
  Remove all data records with \texttt{negative\ BILL\_AMT} values using
  \texttt{DELETE}.
\item
  Select and show the first 10 records in the database table, using
  \texttt{SELECT\ …\ LIMIT…}.
\item
  Select and show all records with a \texttt{BILL\_AMT} amount
  \texttt{\textgreater{}\ 500,000};
\item
  Compute the \textbf{total number of records} \texttt{count(*)},
  average (\texttt{avg}) AGE, \texttt{min} LIMIT\_BAL, \texttt{max}
  LIMIT\_BAL in the data.
\item
  \texttt{Count} the \# records, average AGE, \texttt{min} LIMIT\_BAL,
  \texttt{max} LIMIT\_BAL, using \texttt{GROUP\ BY}, for each group of
  \texttt{DefaultNext} (0 and 1 levels).
\item
  \texttt{Count} the \# records, \texttt{average} AGE, \texttt{min}
  LIMIT\_BAL, \texttt{max} LIMIT\_BAL for each \texttt{Marriage} group
  (1, 2), again using \texttt{GROUP\ BY}.
\item
  Count the \# records in each combination of \texttt{Marriage} groups
  and \texttt{DefaultNext} levels, using
  \texttt{GROUP\ BY\ Marriage,\ DefaultNext}.
\end{enumerate}

For Items 1 and 2 above, you only need to call the cursor's
\texttt{.execute()} method with proper SQL statements to execute.

For Items 3 and after, when you execute the SQL statement, you need to
print the retrieved results using a loop such as:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Say a few words about what you are printing here"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{rows }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ my\_cursor.fetchall()}
\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ row }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ rows}
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(row[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{], row[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{], ...)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section*{Bonus (+1 point)}\label{bonus-1-point-1}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Bonus (+1 point)}

\markright{Bonus (+1 point)}

Organize the above result printing code as a \textbf{function} so that:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi})}
\item
  You can call the function to print all rows and columns each time you
  query the database;
\item
  You reduce redundant code on printing results from item 3 through 8.
\end{enumerate}

\section*{SQLite}\label{sqlite}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{SQLite}

\markright{SQLite}

SQL: structured query language for relational databases

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  SQLite implements a simple SQL dialect
\item
  SQLite uses data files

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    No need to setup a database server
  \end{itemize}
\item
  Widely used and supported, e.g.~on mobile phones
\end{itemize}

\section*{SQLite Interactive}\label{sqlite-interactive}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{SQLite Interactive}

\markright{SQLite Interactive}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  SQLite has a SQL interactive tool

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Please download from: http://www.sqlite.org/download.html
  \item
    Guide to SQLite interpreter: http://sqlite.org/cli.html
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\section*{SQLite Interactive}\label{sqlite-interactive-1}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{SQLite Interactive}

\markright{SQLite Interactive}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Download and install SQLite
\item
  Go to your Terminal or Command Line, and enter:
\end{enumerate}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{sqlite3}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\setcounter{enumi}{2}
\tightlist
\item
  Start using SQLite interactive with

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    dot commands
  \item
    SQL statements
  \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

Here is the interface on the Mac terminal / command line:

Enter \texttt{.help} (a dot command) on SQLite prompt will list all
supported commands.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{sqlite\textgreater{} .help}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section*{\texorpdfstring{Database
\texttt{college.db}}{Database college.db}}\label{database-college.db}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Database \texttt{college.db}}

\markright{Database \texttt{college.db}}

Suppose we are to manage the following data in a college: 1. Degree
programs with ID, program name, and description 2. Students in the
programs, with: ID, name, program information, and class year.

\subsection*{Load SQLite Database}\label{load-sqlite-database}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Load SQLite Database}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%}\NormalTok{sql sqlite:}\OperatorTok{///}\NormalTok{college.db}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Let's open -- create if it does not exist -- a database file called
\texttt{college.db}:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{sqlite\textgreater{} .open college.db}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Screenshot on Mac terminal:

We can now create the two tables using SQL statements with the SQLite3
interactive.

Please note that \texttt{\%\%sql} symbols, for example:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{select }\OperatorTok{*} \ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ my\_table}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

in this tutorial is for SQL magic in the Jupyter Notebook and should
\textbf{be excluded} from your actual SQL statement.

\subsection*{\texorpdfstring{\texttt{programs}
table}{programs table}}\label{programs-table}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{\texttt{programs} table}

Create the \texttt{programs} table structure:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{drop table }\ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ exists programs}\OperatorTok{;}
\NormalTok{create table programs (}
\NormalTok{    program\_id varchar(}\DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{) }\KeywordTok{not}\NormalTok{ null primary key, }
\NormalTok{    program\_name varchar(}\DecValTok{20}\NormalTok{), }
\NormalTok{    program\_desc varchar(}\DecValTok{500}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{)}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Now add (insert) program data:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{insert into programs (program\_id, program\_name, program\_desc)}
\NormalTok{            values   (}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}IS\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Information Systems"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Information systems with a business angle"}\NormalTok{)}\OperatorTok{;}
\NormalTok{insert into programs values (}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}DS\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Data Science"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"New data science program"}\NormalTok{)}\OperatorTok{;}
\NormalTok{insert into programs values }
\NormalTok{        (}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}CS\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Computer Science"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Traditional computer science"}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{        (}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}CST\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Computing \& Security Technology"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"CST with a new focus on security"}\NormalTok{)}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Now let's take a look at data in the table:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{select }\OperatorTok{*} \ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ programs}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsection*{\texorpdfstring{\texttt{students}
table}{students table}}\label{students-table}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{\texttt{students} table}

Create the students table:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{drop table }\ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ exists students}\OperatorTok{;}
\NormalTok{create table students (}
\NormalTok{    student\_id integer primary key, }
\NormalTok{    student\_name varchar(}\DecValTok{100}\NormalTok{), }
\NormalTok{    program\_id varchar(}\DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    class\_year }\BuiltInTok{int}
\NormalTok{)}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

For the students tables, we have preppared a csv file with students
records, which can be downloaded from:
\href{data/students.csv}{students.csv}.

Suppose data file \texttt{students.csv} is in the \textbf{same directory
as the college.db}:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{1   John Smith,        IS,  2020}
\NormalTok{2   Albert Einstein,   DS   2021}
\NormalTok{3   George Washington, CS,  2019}
\NormalTok{4   Donald Trump,      CST, 2020}
\NormalTok{5   Barack Obama,      IS,  2021}
\NormalTok{.   ...                ..   ....}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

You can use the following \textbf{dot commands} to import the CSV data:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{sqlite\textgreater{} .mode csv}
\NormalTok{sqlite\textgreater{} .import students.csv students}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Now check out the data:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{select }\OperatorTok{*} \ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ students limit }\DecValTok{5}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{select count(}\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{) }\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ students}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsection*{Select and Filter}\label{select-and-filter}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Select and Filter}

Now that we have the data, we can go ahead to search the data and run
statistics.

For example, if you are interested in students in the DS program:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{select }\OperatorTok{*} \ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ students where program\_id}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}DS\textquotesingle{}}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Or, you would like to know who have graduated before 2019:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{select }\OperatorTok{*} \ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ students where class\_year}\OperatorTok{\textless{}}\DecValTok{2019}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsection*{Group Aggregates}\label{group-aggregates}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Group Aggregates}

Perhaps, you only want to know statistics in each program:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{select program\_id, }
\NormalTok{       count(}\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{) }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ student\_count, }
       \BuiltInTok{min}\NormalTok{(class\_year) }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ first\_class, }
       \BuiltInTok{max}\NormalTok{(class\_year) }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ last\_class}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ students }
\NormalTok{group by program\_id}
\NormalTok{order by student\_count DESC}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsection*{Update Student Data}\label{update-student-data}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Update Student Data}

Now that you see from the statistics some data values are unrealistic
such as a class year \(>2030\). Perhaps we can reset all these values to
\(2030\) if they are greater than that:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{update students }\BuiltInTok{set}\NormalTok{ class\_year }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{2030}\NormalTok{ where class\_year }\OperatorTok{\textgreater{}} \DecValTok{2030}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

We can run the statistics again to see if data have been updated:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{select program\_id, }
\NormalTok{       count(}\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{) }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ student\_count, }
       \BuiltInTok{min}\NormalTok{(class\_year) }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ first\_class, }
       \BuiltInTok{max}\NormalTok{(class\_year) }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ last\_class}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ students }
\NormalTok{group by program\_id}
\NormalTok{order by student\_count DESC}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsection*{Join Tables}\label{join-tables}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Join Tables}

Suppose you want to retrieve student data with their corresponding
program information (e.g.~program name):

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{select student\_name, program\_name, class\_year}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ students s join programs p on s.program\_id }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ p.program\_id}
\NormalTok{limit }\DecValTok{10}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

We can rerun the previous statistics based on the program names, instead
of program IDs:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\OperatorTok{\%\%}\NormalTok{sql}
\NormalTok{select program\_name, }
\NormalTok{       count(}\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{) }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ student\_count, }
       \BuiltInTok{min}\NormalTok{(class\_year) }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ first\_class, }
       \BuiltInTok{max}\NormalTok{(class\_year) }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ last\_class}
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ students s join programs p on s.program\_id }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ p.program\_id}
\NormalTok{group by program\_name}
\NormalTok{order by student\_count DESC}\OperatorTok{;}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\chapter*{SQLite with Python}\label{ch-lab-sqlite-python}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{SQLite with Python}

\markboth{SQLite with Python}{SQLite with Python}

\section*{Recovered activity}\label{sec-lab-sqlite-python}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Recovered activity}

\markright{Recovered activity}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, arc=.35mm, bottomrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, breakable, colback=white, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-note-color!10!white, colframe=quarto-callout-note-color-frame, coltitle=black, left=2mm, leftrule=.75mm, opacityback=0, opacitybacktitle=0.6, rightrule=.15mm, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-note-color}{\faInfo}\hspace{0.5em}{Historical source and execution note}, titlerule=0mm, toprule=.15mm, toptitle=1mm]

\section*{SQLite with Python}\label{sqlite-with-python}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{SQLite with Python}

\markright{SQLite with Python}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  SQLite: File-based relational SQL database
\item
  Python: A popular language in data science, etc.
\item
  SQLite is well supported in Python
\end{itemize}

This tutorial will follow the same \texttt{college.db} example in the
\hyperref[sec-lab-sqlite]{SQLite Practice} presentation.

\section*{Python Code for SQLite}\label{python-code-for-sqlite}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Python Code for SQLite}

\markright{Python Code for SQLite}

\subsection*{Import SQLite}\label{import-sqlite}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Import SQLite}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ sqlite3}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsection*{Load SQLite Database}\label{load-sqlite-database-1}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Load SQLite Database}

To open and connect to the database file \texttt{college.db}:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{db }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}college.db\textquotesingle{}}
\NormalTok{conn }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ sqlite3.}\ExtensionTok{connect}\NormalTok{(db)}
\NormalTok{c }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ conn.cursor()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

We can now create the two tables:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Programs with ID, program name, and description;
\item
  Students with ID, name, program info, and class year.
\end{enumerate}

using SQL statements with the SQLite3 interactive.

\subsection*{\texorpdfstring{\texttt{programs}
table}{programs table}}\label{programs-table-1}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{\texttt{programs} table}

Create the \texttt{programs} table structure:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{c.execute(}\StringTok{"drop table if exists programs"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{c.execute(}\StringTok{"""create table programs (}
\StringTok{                program\_id varchar(10) not null primary key, }
\StringTok{                program\_name varchar(20), }
\StringTok{                program\_desc varchar(500)}
\StringTok{            )"""}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{conn.commit()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Now we can start adding students data:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{insert\_sql }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{"insert into programs (program\_id, program\_name, program\_desc) values (?, ?, ?)"}

\NormalTok{c.execute(insert\_sql, (}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}IS\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Information Systems\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Information systems with a business angle\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{) )}
\NormalTok{c.execute(insert\_sql, (}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}DS\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Data Science\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}New data science program\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{) ) }
\NormalTok{c.execute(insert\_sql, (}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}CS\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Computer Science\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Traditional computer science\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{) ) }
\NormalTok{c.execute(insert\_sql, (}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}CST\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Computing \& Security Technology\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}CST with a new focus on security\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{) )}

\NormalTok{conn.commit()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Now let's take a look at data in the table:

\subsection*{\texorpdfstring{\texttt{students}
table}{students table}}\label{students-table-1}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{\texttt{students} table}

Create the students table:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{c.execute(}\StringTok{"drop table if exists students"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{c.execute(}\StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    create table students (}
\StringTok{        student\_id integer primary key, }
\StringTok{        student\_name varchar(100), }
\StringTok{        program\_id varchar(10),}
\StringTok{        class\_year int}
\StringTok{    )}
\StringTok{"""}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{conn.commit()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

For the students tables, we have preppared a csv file with students
records, which can be downloaded from:
\href{data/students.csv}{students.csv}.

Suppose data file \texttt{students.csv} is in the \textbf{data}
sub-directory (folder):

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{1   John Smith,        IS,  2020}
\NormalTok{2   Albert Einstein,   DS   2021}
\NormalTok{3   George Washington, CS,  2019}
\NormalTok{4   Donald Trump,      CST, 2020}
\NormalTok{5   Barack Obama,      IS,  2021}
\NormalTok{.   ...                ..   ....}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Let read the CSV file and load data into the \texttt{students} table:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ csv}

\CommentTok{\# remove all student data first}
\NormalTok{delete\_sql }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{"delete from students"}
\NormalTok{c.execute(delete\_sql)}

\CommentTok{\# load CSV data}
\NormalTok{f}\OperatorTok{=}\BuiltInTok{open}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"data/students.csv"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{insert\_sql }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{"insert into students values (?, ?, ?, ?)"}
\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ row }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ csv.reader(f):}
\NormalTok{    c.execute(insert\_sql, row)}
    
\NormalTok{conn.commit()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Now check out the data:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{c.execute(}\StringTok{"select * from students limit 10"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{rows }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ c.fetchall()}
\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ row }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ rows: }
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(row)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Now let's count the number of records in the table:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{c.execute(}\StringTok{"select count(*) from students"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{rows }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ c.fetchall()}
\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ row }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ rows: }
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"The total number of students:"}\NormalTok{, row[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsection*{Group Aggregates}\label{group-aggregates-1}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Group Aggregates}

Perhaps, you only want to know statistics in each program:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{query }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{"""select program\_id, }
\StringTok{       count(*) as student\_count, }
\StringTok{       min(class\_year) as first\_class, }
\StringTok{       max(class\_year) as last\_class}
\StringTok{from students }
\StringTok{group by program\_id}
\StringTok{order by student\_count DESC}
\StringTok{"""}
\NormalTok{c.execute(query)}
\NormalTok{rows }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ c.fetchall()}
\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ row }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ rows: }
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(row[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{], row[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{], row[}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{], row[}\DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{])}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsection*{Update Student Data}\label{update-student-data-1}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Update Student Data}

Now that you see from the statistics some data values are unrealistic
such as a class year \(>2030\). Perhaps we can reset all these values to
\(2030\) if they are greater than that:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{update\_sql }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{"update students set class\_year = 2030 where class\_year \textgreater{} 2030"}
\NormalTok{c.execute(update\_sql)}
\NormalTok{conn.commit()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

We can run the statistics again to see if data have been updated:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{from}\NormalTok{ pprint }\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ pprint}

\NormalTok{query }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{"""select program\_id, }
\StringTok{       count(*) as student\_count, }
\StringTok{       min(class\_year) as first\_class, }
\StringTok{       max(class\_year) as last\_class}
\StringTok{from students }
\StringTok{group by program\_id}
\StringTok{order by student\_count DESC}
\StringTok{"""}
\NormalTok{c.execute(query)}
\NormalTok{rows }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ c.fetchall()}
\NormalTok{pprint(rows)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\subsection*{Join Tables}\label{join-tables-1}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Join Tables}

Suppose you want to retrieve student data with their corresponding
program information (e.g.~program name):

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{query }\OperatorTok{=} \StringTok{"""}
\StringTok{    select student\_name, program\_name, class\_year}
\StringTok{    from students s join programs p }
\StringTok{         on s.program\_id = p.program\_id}
\StringTok{    limit 10}
\StringTok{"""}
\NormalTok{c.execute(query)}
\NormalTok{rows }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ c.fetchall()}
\ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ row }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ rows: }
    \BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"}\SpecialCharTok{\{:s\}}\StringTok{ }\SpecialCharTok{\{:s\}}\StringTok{ }\SpecialCharTok{\{:d\}}\StringTok{"}\NormalTok{.}\BuiltInTok{format}\NormalTok{(row[}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{].ljust(}\DecValTok{20}\NormalTok{), row[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{].ljust(}\DecValTok{40}\NormalTok{), row[}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{]))}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}
